15/06/23, 17:13 - Sriram: The carbon balance method is based on the principle of conservation of mass. According to this principle, matter cannot be created or destroyed, only transformed from one form to another. In the case of a chemical reaction, the total mass of the reactants must be equal to the total mass of the products. This means that the amount of carbon in the starting material must be equal to the amount of carbon in the end product, plus the amount of carbon dioxide released.

To calculate the amount of carbon dioxide released, you need to measure the amount of carbon in the starting material and the end product. This can be done using a variety of methods, such as combustion analysis or mass spectrometry. Once you have these values, you can subtract the amount of carbon in the end product from the amount of carbon in the starting material to get the amount of carbon dioxide released.

It's important to note that the carbon balance method assumes that all of the carbon in the starting material is accounted for in the end product and the carbon dioxide released. In reality, there may be other byproducts or side reactions that can complicate the analysis. Additionally, the carbon balance method only gives information about the amount of carbon dioxide released, not other greenhouse gases or pollutants that may be produced during a reaction.
15/06/23, 17:19 - Sriram: Example---

| Stream | Carbon (g) |
|--------|------------|
| Starting Material | 100 |
| End Product | 90 |
| Byproduct 1 | 5 |
| Byproduct 2 | 3 |
| Waste | 2 |
you could calculate the amount of carbon dioxide released by subtracting the carbon in the end product from the carbon in the starting material:

Carbon dioxide released = Starting material carbon - End product carbon
Carbon dioxide released = 100 g - 90 g
Carbon dioxide released = 10 g
